<div style="text-align: center;"><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paramount_leader_(China)" title="Paramount leader (China)">Paramount Leader of <br/>the People's Republic of China</a></b><br/>
<div class="hlist hlist-separated">
<ul><li>(<i>Inaugural holder</i>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hua_Guofeng" title="Hua Guofeng">Hua Guofeng</a> <span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>→</b></span></li></ul>
</div></div></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-below" colspan="2" style="border-top: 1px solid right; font-size: 95%"><div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Mao Zedong</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[a]</a></sup> (26 December 1893 – 9 September 1976), also known as <b>Chairman Mao</b>, was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_communist" title="Chinese communist">Chinese communist</a> <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">revolutionary</a> who was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_founders" title="List of national founders">founder</a> of the People's Republic of China (PRC), which he led as the <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chairman of the Chinese Communist Party">chairman of the Chinese Communist Party</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Establishment_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Establishment of the People's Republic of China">establishment of the PRC</a> in 1949 until <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Mao_Zedong" title="Death and state funeral of Mao Zedong">his death</a> in 1976. Ideologically a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist" title="Marxist–Leninist">Marxist–Leninist</a>, his theories, military strategies, and political policies are collectively known as <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoism</a>.
</p><p>Mao was the son of a prosperous peasant in <a href="/wiki/Shaoshan" title="Shaoshan">Shaoshan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a>. He supported <a href="/wiki/Chinese_nationalism" title="Chinese nationalism">Chinese nationalism</a> and had an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-imperialist" title="Anti-imperialist">anti-imperialist</a> outlook early in his life, and was particularly influenced by the events of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a> of 1911 and <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> of 1919. He later adopted Marxism–Leninism while working at <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a> as a librarian and became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party" title="Chinese Communist Party">Chinese Communist Party</a> (CCP), leading the <a href="/wiki/Autumn_Harvest_Uprising" title="Autumn Harvest Uprising">Autumn Harvest Uprising</a> in 1927. During the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT) and the CCP, Mao helped to found the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Workers%27_and_Peasants%27_Red_Army" title="Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army">Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army</a>, led the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jiangxi_Soviet" title="Jiangxi Soviet">Jiangxi Soviet</a>'s radical land policies, and ultimately became head of the CCP during the <a href="/wiki/Long_March" title="Long March">Long March</a>. Although the CCP temporarily allied with the KMT under the <a href="/wiki/Second_United_Front" title="Second United Front">Second United Front</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a> (1937–1945), China's civil war resumed after <a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan_Day" title="Victory over Japan Day">Japan's surrender</a>, and Mao's forces defeated the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_government" title="Nationalist government">Nationalist government</a>, which withdrew to <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> in 1949.
</p><p>On 1 October 1949, Mao <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Proclamation of the People's Republic of China">proclaimed the foundation of the PRC</a>, a Marxist–Leninist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single-party_state" title="Single-party state">single-party state</a> controlled by the CCP. In the following years he solidified his control through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_Land_Reform" title="Chinese Land Reform">Chinese Land Reform</a> against landlords, the <a href="/wiki/Campaign_to_Suppress_Counterrevolutionaries" title="Campaign to Suppress Counterrevolutionaries">Campaign to Suppress Counterrevolutionaries</a>, the "<a href="/wiki/Three-anti_and_Five-anti_Campaigns" title="Three-anti and Five-anti Campaigns">Three-anti and Five-anti Campaigns</a>", and through a psychological victory in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, which altogether resulted in the deaths of several million Chinese. From 1953 to 1958, Mao played an important role in enforcing <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">planned economy</a> in China, constructing the <a href="/wiki/1954_Constitution_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="1954 Constitution of the People's Republic of China">first Constitution of the PRC</a>, launching the industrialisation <a href="/wiki/Industry_of_China" title="Industry of China">program</a>, and initiating military projects such as the "<a href="/wiki/Two_Bombs,_One_Satellite" title="Two Bombs, One Satellite">Two Bombs, One Satellite</a>" project and <a href="/wiki/Project_523" title="Project 523">Project 523</a>. His foreign policies during this time were dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">Sino-Soviet split</a> which drove a wedge between China and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. In 1955, Mao launched the <a href="/wiki/Sufan_movement" title="Sufan movement">Sufan movement</a>, and in 1957 he launched the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Rightist_Campaign" title="Anti-Rightist Campaign">Anti-Rightist Campaign</a>, in which at least 550,000 people, mostly intellectuals and dissidents, were persecuted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1Mac_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-1Mac-3">[2]</a></sup> In 1958, he launched the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> that aimed to rapidly transform China's economy from <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_society" title="Agrarian society">agrarian</a> to <a href="/wiki/Industrial_society" title="Industrial society">industrial</a>, which led to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chinese_Famine" title="Great Chinese Famine">deadliest famine in history</a> and the deaths of 15–55 million people between 1958 and 1962. In 1963, Mao launched the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Education_Movement" title="Socialist Education Movement">Socialist Education Movement</a>, and in 1966 he initiated the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Revolution" title="Cultural Revolution">Cultural Revolution</a>, a program to remove "counter-revolutionary" elements in Chinese society which lasted 10 years and was marked by violent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_struggle" title="Class struggle">class struggle</a>, widespread destruction of cultural artifacts, and an unprecedented elevation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mao%27s_cult_of_personality" title="Mao's cult of personality">Mao's cult of personality</a>. Tens of millions of people were persecuted during the Revolution, while the estimated number of deaths ranges from hundreds of thousands to millions. After years of ill health, Mao suffered a series of heart attacks in 1976 and died at the age of 82. During Mao's era, China's population grew from around 550 million to over 900 million while the government did not strictly enforce its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_planning_policy" title="Family planning policy">family planning policy</a>.
</p><p>A controversial figure within and outside China, Mao is still regarded as one of the most influential figures of the twentieth century. Beyond politics, Mao is also known as a theorist, military strategist, and poet. During the Mao era, China was heavily involved with other southeast Asian communist conflicts such as the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Civil_War" title="Cambodian Civil War">Cambodian Civil War</a>, which brought the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> to power. He ruled China through an autocratic and totalitarian regime responsible for mass repression as well as destruction of religious and cultural artifacts and sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-4">[3]</a></sup> The government was responsible for vast numbers of deaths with estimates ranging from 40 to 80 million victims through starvation, persecution, <a href="/wiki/Laogai" title="Laogai">prison labour</a>, and mass executions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-6">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> Mao has been praised for transforming China from a <a href="/wiki/Semi-colony" title="Semi-colony">semi-colony</a> to a leading world power, with greatly advanced literacy, women's rights, basic healthcare, primary education and life expectancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galtung_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Galtung-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopulationStudies2015_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-PopulationStudies2015-12">[11]</a></sup>
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English_romanisation_of_name">English romanisation of name</span></h2>
<p>During Mao's lifetime, the English-language media universally rendered his name as Mao Tse-tung, using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wade-Giles" title="Wade-Giles">Wade-Giles</a> system of transliteration for Standard Chinese though with the circumflex accent in the syllable <i>Tsê</i> dropped. Due to its recognizability, the spelling was used widely, even by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Ministry_of_the_PRC" title="Foreign Ministry of the PRC">Foreign Ministry of the PRC</a> after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a> became the PRC's official romanisation system for <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a> in 1958; the well-known booklet of Mao's political statements, <i><a href="/wiki/Quotations_from_Chairman_Mao_Tse-tung" title="Quotations from Chairman Mao Tse-tung">The Little Red Book</a></i>, was officially entitled <i>Quotations from Chairman Mao Tse-tung</i> in English translations. While the pinyin-derived spelling <i>Mao Zedong</i> is increasingly common, the Wade-Giles-derived spelling <i>Mao Tse-tung</i> continues to be used in modern publications to some extent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_life_of_Mao_Zedong" title="Early life of Mao Zedong">Early life of Mao Zedong</a></div>
<h3><span id="Youth_and_the_Xinhai_Revolution:_1893.E2.80.931911"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_and_the_Xinhai_Revolution:_1893–1911">Youth and the Xinhai Revolution: 1893–1911</span></h3>
<p>Mao Zedong was born on 26 December 1893, in <a href="/wiki/Shaoshan" title="Shaoshan">Shaoshan</a> village, <a href="/wiki/Hunan" title="Hunan">Hunan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchram196619Hollingworth198515PantsovLevine201211_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchram196619Hollingworth198515PantsovLevine201211-14">[13]</a></sup> His father, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Yichang" title="Mao Yichang">Mao Yichang</a>, was a formerly impoverished peasant who had become one of the wealthiest farmers in Shaoshan. Growing up in rural Hunan, Mao described his father as a stern disciplinarian, who would beat him and his three siblings, the boys <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zemin" title="Mao Zemin">Zemin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zetan" title="Mao Zetan">Zetan</a>, as well as an adopted girl, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zejian" title="Mao Zejian">Zejian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> Mao's mother, <a href="/wiki/Wen_Qimei" title="Wen Qimei">Wen Qimei</a>, was a devout <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddhist" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> who tried to temper her husband's strict attitude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11-16">[15]</a></sup> Mao too became a Buddhist, but abandoned this faith in his mid-teenage years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p20_Terrill_1980_11-16">[15]</a></sup> At age 8, Mao was sent to Shaoshan Primary School. Learning the value systems of <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, he later admitted that he did not enjoy the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_classics" title="Chinese classics">classical Chinese texts</a> preaching Confucian morals, instead favouring <a href="/wiki/Classic_Chinese_Novels" title="Classic Chinese Novels">classic novels</a> like <i><a href="/wiki/Romance_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" title="Romance of the Three Kingdoms">Romance of the Three Kingdoms</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Water_Margin" title="Water Margin">Water Margin</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> At age 13, Mao finished primary education, and his father united him in an <a href="/wiki/Arranged_marriage" title="Arranged marriage">arranged marriage</a> to the 17-year-old <a href="/wiki/Luo_Yixiu" title="Luo Yixiu">Luo Yixiu</a>, thereby uniting their land-owning families. Mao refused to recognise her as his wife, becoming a fierce critic of arranged marriage and temporarily moving away. Luo was locally disgraced and died in 1910, at only 21 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shaoshan_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="3328" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shaoshan_01.JPG/220px-Shaoshan_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shaoshan_01.JPG/330px-Shaoshan_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Shaoshan_01.JPG/440px-Shaoshan_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shaoshan_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Former_Residence_of_Mao_Zedong" title="Former Residence of Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong's childhood home</a> in Shaoshan, in 2010, by which time it had become a tourist destination</div></div></div>
<p>While working on his father's farm, Mao read voraciously<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> and developed a "political consciousness" from <a href="/wiki/Zheng_Guanying" title="Zheng Guanying">Zheng Guanying</a>'s booklet which lamented the deterioration of Chinese power and argued for the adoption of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> Interested in history, Mao was inspired by the military prowess and nationalistic fervour of <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> His political views were shaped by <a href="/wiki/Gelaohui" title="Gelaohui">Gelaohui</a>-led protests which erupted following a famine in <a href="/wiki/Changsha" title="Changsha">Changsha</a>, the capital of Hunan; Mao supported the protesters' demands, but the armed forces suppressed the dissenters and executed their leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The famine spread to Shaoshan, where starving peasants seized his father's grain. He disapproved of their actions as morally wrong, but claimed sympathy for their situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> At age 16, Mao moved to a higher primary school in nearby Dongshan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> where he was bullied for his peasant background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1911, Mao began middle school in Changsha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Revolutionary sentiment was strong in the city, where there was widespread animosity towards Emperor <a href="/wiki/Puyi" title="Puyi">Puyi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a> and many were advocating <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a>. The republicans' figurehead was <a href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen" title="Sun Yat-sen">Sun Yat-sen</a>, an American-educated Christian who led the <a href="/wiki/Tongmenghui" title="Tongmenghui">Tongmenghui</a> society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In Changsha, Mao was influenced by Sun's newspaper, <i>The People's Independence</i> (<i>Minli bao</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> and called for Sun to become president in a school essay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> As a symbol of rebellion against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">Manchu</a> monarch, Mao and a friend cut off their <a href="/wiki/Queue_(hairstyle)" title="Queue (hairstyle)">queue</a> pigtails, a sign of subservience to the emperor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Inspired by Sun's republicanism, the army rose up across southern China, sparking the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinhai_Revolution" title="Xinhai Revolution">Xinhai Revolution</a>. Changsha's governor fled, leaving the city in republican control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> Supporting the revolution, Mao joined the rebel army as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_soldier" title="Private soldier">private soldier</a>, but was not involved in fighting. The northern provinces remained loyal to the emperor, and hoping to avoid a civil war, Sun—proclaimed "provisional president" by his supporters—compromised with the monarchist general <a href="/wiki/Yuan_Shikai" title="Yuan Shikai">Yuan Shikai</a>. The monarchy was abolished, creating the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949)" title="Republic of China (1912–1949)">Republic of China</a>, but the monarchist Yuan became president. The revolution over, Mao resigned from the army in 1912, after six months as a soldier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Around this time, Mao discovered <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> from a newspaper article; proceeding to read pamphlets by <a href="/wiki/Jiang_Kanghu" title="Jiang Kanghu">Jiang Kanghu</a>, the student founder of the Chinese Socialist Party, Mao remained interested yet unconvinced by the idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Fourth_Normal_School_of_Changsha:_1912.E2.80.931919"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_Normal_School_of_Changsha:_1912–1919">Fourth Normal School of Changsha: 1912–1919</span></h3>
<p>Over the next few years, Mao Zedong enrolled and dropped out of a police academy, a soap-production school, a law school, an economics school, and the government-run <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Changsha_Middle_School" title="Changsha Middle School">Changsha Middle School</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> Studying independently, he spent much time in Changsha's library, reading core works of <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberalism</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wealth_of_Nations" title="The Wealth of Nations">The Wealth of Nations</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Montesquieu" title="Montesquieu">Montesquieu</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Spirit_of_the_Laws" title="The Spirit of the Laws">The Spirit of the Laws</a></i>, as well as the works of western scientists and philosophers such as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Darwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">Mill</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rousseau" title="Rousseau">Rousseau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Spencer" title="Herbert Spencer">Spencer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> Viewing himself as an intellectual, years later he admitted that at this time he thought himself better than working people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> He was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Paulsen" title="Friedrich Paulsen">Friedrich Paulsen</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Neo-Kantianism" title="Neo-Kantianism">neo-Kantian</a> philosopher and educator whose emphasis on the achievement of a carefully defined goal as the highest value led Mao to believe that strong individuals were not bound by moral codes but should strive for a great goal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> His father saw no use in his son's intellectual pursuits, cut off his allowance and forced him to move into a hostel for the destitute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="996" decoding="async" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg/170px-Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg/255px-Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg/340px-Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao_Zedong_1913.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mao in 1913</div></div></div>
<p>Mao desired to become a teacher and enrolled at the Fourth Normal School of Changsha, which soon merged with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Normal_School_of_Hunan" title="First Normal School of Hunan">First Normal School of Hunan</a>, widely seen as the best in Hunan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Befriending Mao, professor <a href="/wiki/Yang_Changji" title="Yang Changji">Yang Changji</a> urged him to read a radical newspaper, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Jeunesse" title="La Jeunesse">New Youth</a></i> (<i>Xin qingnian</i>), the creation of his friend <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a>, a dean at <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>. Although he was a supporter of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_nationalism" title="Chinese nationalism">Chinese nationalism</a>, Chen argued that China must look to the west to cleanse itself of superstition and autocracy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup>
In his first school year, Mao befriended an older student, <a href="/wiki/Xiao_Zisheng" title="Xiao Zisheng">Xiao Zisheng</a>; together they went on a walking tour of Hunan, begging and writing literary couplets to obtain food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>A popular student, in 1915 Mao was elected secretary of the Students Society. He organised the Association for Student Self-Government and led protests against school rules.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Mao published his first article in <i>New Youth</i> in April 1917, instructing readers to increase their physical strength to serve the revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> He joined the Society for the Study of Wang Fuzhi (<i>Chuan-shan Hsüeh-she</i>), a revolutionary group founded by Changsha literati who wished to emulate the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Wang_Fuzhi" title="Wang Fuzhi">Wang Fuzhi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> In spring 1917, he was elected to command the students' volunteer army, set up to defend the school from marauding soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Increasingly interested in the techniques of war, he took a keen interest in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, and also began to develop a sense of solidarity with workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Mao undertook feats of physical endurance with Xiao Zisheng and <a href="/wiki/Cai_Hesen" title="Cai Hesen">Cai Hesen</a>, and with other young revolutionaries they formed the Renovation of the People Study Society in April 1918 to debate Chen Duxiu's ideas. Desiring personal and societal transformation, the Society gained 70–80 members, many of whom would later join the Communist Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Mao graduated in June 1919, ranked third in the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_revolutionary_activity">Early revolutionary activity</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Beijing.2C_anarchism.2C_and_Marxism:_1917.E2.80.931919"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Beijing,_anarchism,_and_Marxism:_1917–1919">Beijing, anarchism, and Marxism: 1917–1919</span></h3>
<p>Mao moved to Beijing, where his mentor Yang Changji had taken a job at Peking University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Yang thought Mao exceptionally "intelligent and handsome",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> securing him a job as assistant to the university librarian <a href="/wiki/Li_Dazhao" title="Li Dazhao">Li Dazhao</a>, who would become an early Chinese Communist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> Li authored a series of <i>New Youth</i> articles on the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> in Russia, during which the Communist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik_Party" title="Bolshevik Party">Bolshevik Party</a> under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> had seized power. Lenin was an advocate of the socio-political theory of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a>, first developed by the German sociologists <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">Friedrich Engels</a>, and Li's articles added Marxism to the doctrines in Chinese revolutionary movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>Becoming "more and more radical", Mao was initially influenced by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a>, which was the most prominent radical doctrine of the day. <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_China" title="Anarchism in China">Chinese anarchists</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Cai_Yuanpei" title="Cai Yuanpei">Cai Yuanpei</a>, Chancellor of Peking University, called for complete social revolution in social relations, family structure, and women's equality, rather than the simple change in the form of government called for by earlier revolutionaries. He joined Li's Study Group and "developed rapidly toward Marxism" during the winter of 1919.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Paid a low wage, Mao lived in a cramped room with seven other Hunanese students, but believed that Beijing's beauty offered "vivid and living compensation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> A number of his friends took advantage of the anarchist-organised <i>Mouvement Travail-Études</i> to study in France, but Mao declined, perhaps because of an inability to learn languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the university, Mao was snubbed by other students due to his rural Hunanese accent and lowly position. He joined the university's Philosophy and Journalism Societies and attended lectures and seminars by the likes of <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hu_Shih" title="Hu Shih">Hu Shih</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qian_Xuantong" title="Qian Xuantong">Qian Xuantong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> Mao's time in Beijing ended in the spring of 1919, when he travelled to Shanghai with friends who were preparing to leave for France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> He did not return to Shaoshan, where his mother was terminally ill. She died in October 1919 and her husband died in January 1920.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="New_Culture_and_political_protests:_1919.E2.80.931920"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Culture_and_political_protests:_1919–1920">New Culture and political protests: 1919–1920</span></h3>
<p>On 4 May 1919, students in Beijing gathered at the <a href="/wiki/Tiananmen" title="Tiananmen">Tiananmen</a> to protest the Chinese government's weak resistance to Japanese expansion in China. Patriots were outraged at the influence given to Japan in the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-One_Demands" title="Twenty-One Demands">Twenty-One Demands</a> in 1915, the complicity of <a href="/wiki/Duan_Qirui" title="Duan Qirui">Duan Qirui</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beiyang_Government" title="Beiyang Government">Beiyang Government</a>, and the betrayal of China in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, wherein Japan was allowed to <a href="/wiki/Shandong_Problem" title="Shandong Problem">receive territories in Shandong</a> which had been surrendered by <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>. These demonstrations ignited the nationwide <a href="/wiki/May_Fourth_Movement" title="May Fourth Movement">May Fourth Movement</a> and fuelled the <a href="/wiki/New_Culture_Movement" title="New Culture Movement">New Culture Movement</a> which blamed China's diplomatic defeats on social and cultural backwardness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Changsha, Mao had begun teaching history at the Xiuye Primary School<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup> and organising protests against the pro-Duan Governor of Hunan Province, <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Jingyao" title="Zhang Jingyao">Zhang Jingyao</a>, popularly known as "Zhang the Venomous" due to his corrupt and violent rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> In late May, Mao co-founded the Hunanese Student Association with <a href="/wiki/He_Shuheng" title="He Shuheng">He Shuheng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deng_Zhongxia" title="Deng Zhongxia">Deng Zhongxia</a>, organising a student strike for June and in July 1919 began production of a weekly radical magazine, <i>Xiang River Review</i> (<i>Xiangjiang pinglun</i>). Using vernacular language that would be understandable to the majority of China's populace, he advocated the need for a "Great Union of the Popular Masses", strengthened trade unions able to wage non-violent revolution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> His ideas were not Marxist, but heavily influenced by Kropotkin's concept of <a href="/wiki/Mutual_Aid:_A_Factor_of_Evolution" title="Mutual Aid: A Factor of Evolution">mutual aid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_(May_4,_1919).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="485" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/220px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/330px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg/440px-Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_%28May_4%2C_1919%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Beijing_students_protesting_the_Treaty_of_Versailles_(May_4,_1919).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Students in Beijing rallying during the May Fourth Movement</div></div></div>
<p>Zhang banned the Student Association, but Mao continued publishing after assuming editorship of the liberal magazine <i>New Hunan</i> (<i>Xin Hunan</i>) and offered articles in popular local newspaper <i>Justice</i> (<i>Ta Kung Po</i>). Several of these advocated <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminist</a> views, calling for the liberation of women in Chinese society; Mao was influenced by his forced arranged-marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> In December 1919, Mao helped organise a general strike in Hunan, securing some concessions, but Mao and other student leaders felt threatened by Zhang, and Mao returned to Beijing, visiting the terminally ill Yang Changji.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Mao found that his articles had achieved a level of fame among the revolutionary movement, and set about soliciting support in overthrowing Zhang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> Coming across newly translated Marxist literature by Thomas Kirkup, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Kautsky" title="Karl Kautsky">Karl Kautsky</a>, and Marx and Engels—notably <i><a href="/wiki/The_Communist_Manifesto" title="The Communist Manifesto">The Communist Manifesto</a></i>—he came under their increasing influence, but was still eclectic in his views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mao visited Tianjin, <a href="/wiki/Jinan" title="Jinan">Jinan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qufu" title="Qufu">Qufu</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> before moving to Shanghai, where he worked as a laundryman and met <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a>, noting that Chen's adoption of Marxism "deeply impressed me at what was probably a critical period in my life". In Shanghai, Mao met an old teacher of his, <a href="/wiki/Yi_Peiji" title="Yi Peiji">Yi Peiji</a>, a revolutionary and member of the <a href="/wiki/Kuomintang" title="Kuomintang">Kuomintang</a> (KMT), or Chinese Nationalist Party, which was gaining increasing support and influence. Yi introduced Mao to General <a href="/wiki/Tan_Yankai" title="Tan Yankai">Tan Yankai</a>, a senior KMT member who held the loyalty of troops stationed along the Hunanese border with Guangdong. Tan was plotting to overthrow Zhang, and Mao aided him by organising the Changsha students. In June 1920, Tan led his troops into Changsha, and Zhang fled. In the subsequent reorganisation of the provincial administration, Mao was appointed headmaster of the junior section of the First Normal School. Now receiving a large income, he married Yang Kaihui, daughter of Yang Changji, in the winter of 1920.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mair_2013_p211_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mair_2013_p211-69">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Founding_the_Chinese_Communist_Party:_1921.E2.80.931922"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_the_Chinese_Communist_Party:_1921–1922">Founding the Chinese Communist Party: 1921–1922</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2385" data-file-width="1706" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg/170px-Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg/255px-Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg/340px-Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Location_of_the_First_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party_Xintiandi_Shanghai_July_1921.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the first Congress of the Chinese Communist Party in July 1921, in <a href="/wiki/Xintiandi" title="Xintiandi">Xintiandi</a>, former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Concession" title="French Concession">French Concession</a>, Shanghai</div></div></div>
<p>The Chinese Communist Party was founded by <a href="/wiki/Chen_Duxiu" title="Chen Duxiu">Chen Duxiu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li_Dazhao" title="Li Dazhao">Li Dazhao</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_concession" title="French concession">French concession</a> of Shanghai in 1921 as a study society and informal network. Mao set up a Changsha branch, also establishing a branch of the Socialist Youth Corps and a Cultural Book Society which opened a bookstore to propagate revolutionary literature throughout Hunan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> He was involved in the movement for Hunan autonomy, in the hope that a Hunanese constitution would increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_liberty" title="Civil liberty">civil liberties</a> and make his revolutionary activity easier. When the movement was successful in establishing provincial autonomy under a new warlord, Mao forgot his involvement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> By 1921, small Marxist groups existed in Shanghai, Beijing, Changsha, Wuhan, Guangzhou, and Jinan; it was decided to hold a central meeting, which began in Shanghai on 23 July 1921. The first session of the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_the_Chinese_Communist_Party" title="National Congress of the Chinese Communist Party">National Congress of the Chinese Communist Party</a> was attended by 13 delegates, Mao included. After the authorities sent a police spy to the congress, the delegates moved to a boat on South Lake near <a href="/wiki/Jiaxing" title="Jiaxing">Jiaxing</a>, in Zhejiang, to escape detection. Although Soviet and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern">Comintern</a> delegates attended, the first congress ignored Lenin's advice to accept a temporary alliance between the Communists and the "bourgeois democrats" who also advocated national revolution; instead they stuck to the orthodox Marxist belief that only the urban proletariat could lead a socialist revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mao was now party secretary for Hunan stationed in Changsha, and to build the party there he followed a variety of tactics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p68_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p68-73">[72]</a></sup> In August 1921, he founded the Self-Study University, through which readers could gain access to revolutionary literature, housed in the premises of the Society for the Study of <a href="/wiki/Wang_Fuzhi" title="Wang Fuzhi">Wang Fuzhi</a>, a Qing dynasty Hunanese philosopher who had resisted the Manchus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p68_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p68-73">[72]</a></sup> He joined the <a href="/wiki/YMCA" title="YMCA">YMCA</a> Mass Education Movement to fight illiteracy, though he edited the textbooks to include radical sentiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> He continued organising workers to strike against the administration of Hunan Governor <a href="/wiki/Zhao_Hengti" title="Zhao Hengti">Zhao Hengti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> Yet labour issues remained central. The successful and famous <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anyuan_coal_mines_strikes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anyuan coal mines strikes (page does not exist)">Anyuan coal mines strikes</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://zh.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%AE%89%E6%BA%90%E8%B7%AF%E7%9F%BF%E5%B7%A5%E4%BA%BA%E5%A4%A7%E7%BD%A2%E5%B7%A5" title="zh:安源路矿工人大罢工">zh</a>]</span> (contrary to later Party historians) depended on both "proletarian" and "bourgeois" strategies. <a href="/wiki/Liu_Shaoqi" title="Liu Shaoqi">Liu Shaoqi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li_Lisan" title="Li Lisan">Li Lisan</a> and Mao not only mobilised the miners, but formed schools and cooperatives and engaged local intellectuals, gentry, military officers, merchants, Red Gang dragon heads and even church clergy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mao claimed that he missed the July 1922 Second Congress of the Communist Party in Shanghai because he lost the address. Adopting Lenin's advice, the delegates agreed to an alliance with the "bourgeois democrats" of the KMT for the good of the "national revolution". Communist Party members joined the KMT, hoping to push its politics leftward.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup>
Mao enthusiastically agreed with this decision, arguing for an alliance across China's socio-economic classes, and eventually rose to become propaganda chief of the KMT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mair_2013_p211_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mair_2013_p211-69">[68]</a></sup> Mao was a vocal anti-imperialist and in his writings he lambasted the governments of Japan, the UK and US, describing the latter as "the most murderous of hangmen".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Collaboration_with_the_Kuomintang:_1922.E2.80.931927"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaboration_with_the_Kuomintang:_1922–1927">Collaboration with the Kuomintang: 1922–1927</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><video class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="26" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Chairman_Mao-1.webm" height="165" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Chairman_Mao-1.webm/220px--Chairman_Mao-1.webm.jpg" preload="none" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="512504" data-framerate="25" data-height="360" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="480" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/5b/Chairman_Mao-1.webm/Chairman_Mao-1.webm.360p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="143192" data-framerate="25" data-height="160" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/5b/Chairman_Mao-1.webm/Chairman_Mao-1.webm.160p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="262592" data-framerate="25" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/5b/Chairman_Mao-1.webm/Chairman_Mao-1.webm.240p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="302704" data-framerate="25" data-height="240" data-shorttitle="VP9 240P" data-title="Small VP9 (240P)" data-transcodekey="240p.vp9.webm" data-width="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/5/5b/Chairman_Mao-1.webm/Chairman_Mao-1.webm.240p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chairman_Mao-1.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mao giving speeches to the masses</div></div></div>
<p>At the Third Congress of the Communist Party in Shanghai in June 1923, the delegates reaffirmed their commitment to working with the KMT. Supporting this position, Mao was elected to the Party Committee, taking up residence in Shanghai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> At the First KMT Congress, held in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> in early 1924, Mao was elected an alternate member of the KMT Central Executive Committee, and put forward four resolutions to decentralise power to urban and rural bureaus. His enthusiastic support for the KMT earned him the suspicion of Li Li-san, his Hunan comrade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 1924, Mao returned to Shaoshan, perhaps to recuperate from an illness. He found that the peasantry were increasingly restless and some had seized land from wealthy landowners to found communes. This convinced him of the revolutionary potential of the peasantry, an idea advocated by the KMT leftists but not the Communists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> He returned to Guangzhou to run the 6th term of the KMT's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peasant_Movement_Training_Institute_at_Guangzhou" title="Peasant Movement Training Institute at Guangzhou">Peasant Movement Training Institute</a> from May to September 1926.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> The Peasant Movement Training Institute under Mao trained cadre and prepared them for militant activity, taking them through military training exercises and getting them to study basic left-wing texts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> In the winter of 1925, Mao fled to Guangzhou after his revolutionary activities attracted the attention of Zhao's regional authorities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao_1925.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Mao_1925.jpg/220px-Mao_1925.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/Mao_1925.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao_1925.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mao Zedong around the time of his work at Guangzhou's <a href="/wiki/Peasant_Movement_Training_Institute" title="Peasant Movement Training Institute">PMTI</a> in 1925</div></div></div>
<p>When party leader Sun Yat-sen died in May 1925, he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Chiang_Kai-shek" title="Chiang Kai-shek">Chiang Kai-shek</a>, who moved to marginalise the left-KMT and the Communists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> Mao nevertheless supported Chiang's <a href="/wiki/National_Revolutionary_Army" title="National Revolutionary Army">National Revolutionary Army</a>, who embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Expedition" title="Northern Expedition">Northern Expedition</a> attack in 1926 on warlords.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> In the wake of this expedition, peasants rose up, appropriating the land of the wealthy landowners, who were in many cases killed. Such uprisings angered senior KMT figures, who were themselves landowners, emphasising the growing class and ideological divide within the revolutionary movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="968" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg/220px-KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg/330px-KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg/440px-KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KMT_3rd_Plenary_Session_of_2nd_Central_Committee.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Third Plenum of the KMT Central Executive Committee in March 1927. Mao is third from the right in the second row.</div></div></div>
<p>In March 1927, Mao appeared at the Third Plenum of the KMT Central Executive Committee in Wuhan, which sought to strip General Chiang of his power by appointing <a href="/wiki/Wang_Jingwei" title="Wang Jingwei">Wang Jingwei</a> leader. There, Mao played an active role in the discussions regarding the peasant issue, defending a set of "Regulations for the Repression of Local Bullies and Bad Gentry", which advocated the death penalty or life imprisonment for anyone found guilty of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter-revolution" title="Counter-revolution">counter-revolutionary</a> activity, arguing that in a revolutionary situation, "peaceful methods cannot suffice".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_42_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_42-90">[89]</a></sup> In April 1927, Mao was appointed to the KMT's five-member Central Land Committee, urging peasants to refuse to pay rent. Mao led another group to put together a "Draft Resolution on the Land Question", which called for the confiscation of land belonging to "local bullies and bad gentry, corrupt officials, militarists and all counter-revolutionary elements in the villages". Proceeding to carry out a "Land Survey", he stated that anyone owning over 30 <i>mou</i> (four and a half acres), constituting 13% of the population, were uniformly counter-revolutionary. He accepted that there was great variation in revolutionary enthusiasm across the country, and that a flexible policy of land redistribution was necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Presenting his conclusions at the Enlarged Land Committee meeting, many expressed reservations, some believing that it went too far, and others not far enough. Ultimately, his suggestions were only partially implemented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War">Civil War</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Revolution" title="Chinese Communist Revolution">Chinese Communist Revolution</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nanchang_and_Autumn_Harvest_Uprisings:_1927">Nanchang and Autumn Harvest Uprisings: 1927</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/220px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/330px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg/440px-%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%AD%E5%9C%8B%E5%B7%A5%E8%BE%B2%E7%B4%85%E8%BB%8D%E8%BB%8D%E6%97%97.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People's_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Chinese Workers' and Peasants' Red Army</a></div></div></div>
<p>Fresh from the success of the Northern Expedition against the warlords, Chiang turned on the Communists, who by now numbered in the tens of thousands across China. Chiang ignored the orders of the Wuhan-based left KMT government and marched on Shanghai, a city controlled by Communist militias. As the Communists awaited Chiang's arrival, he loosed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Terror_(mainland_China)" title="White Terror (mainland China)">White Terror</a>, massacring 5000 with the aid of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Gang" title="Green Gang">Green Gang</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_42_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_42-90">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> In Beijing, 19 leading Communists were killed by <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Zuolin" title="Zhang Zuolin">Zhang Zuolin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p62_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p62-95">[94]</a></sup> That May, tens of thousands of Communists and those suspected of being communists were killed, and the CCP lost approximately 15,000 of its 25,000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p62_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p62-95">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>The CCP continued supporting the Wuhan KMT government, a position Mao initially supported,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p62_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p62-95">[94]</a></sup> but by the time of the CCP's Fifth Congress he had changed his mind, deciding to stake all hope on the peasant militia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p63_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p63-96">[95]</a></sup> The question was rendered moot when the Wuhan government expelled all Communists from the KMT on 15 July.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p63_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p63-96">[95]</a></sup> The CCP founded the Workers' and Peasants' Red Army of China, better known as the "<a href="/wiki/History_of_the_People%27s_Liberation_Army#From_the_founding_of_the_People's_Liberation_Army_to_the_Korean_War" title="History of the People's Liberation Army">Red Army</a>", to battle Chiang. A battalion led by General <a href="/wiki/Zhu_De" title="Zhu De">Zhu De</a> was ordered to take the city of <a href="/wiki/Nanchang" title="Nanchang">Nanchang</a> on 1 August 1927, in what became known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanchang_Uprising" title="Nanchang Uprising">Nanchang Uprising</a>. They were initially successful, but were forced into retreat after five days, marching south to <a href="/wiki/Shantou" title="Shantou">Shantou</a>, and from there they were driven into the wilderness of <a href="/wiki/Fujian" title="Fujian">Fujian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p63_96-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p63-96">[95]</a></sup> Mao was appointed commander-in-chief of the Red Army and led four regiments against Changsha in the <a href="/wiki/Autumn_Harvest_Uprising" title="Autumn Harvest Uprising">Autumn Harvest Uprising</a>, in the hope of sparking peasant uprisings across Hunan. On the eve of the attack, Mao composed a poem—the earliest of his to survive—titled "Changsha". His plan was to attack the KMT-held city from three directions on 9 September, but the Fourth Regiment deserted to the KMT cause, attacking the Third Regiment. Mao's army made it to Changsha, but could not take it; by 15 September, he accepted defeat and with 1000 survivors marched east to the <a href="/wiki/Jinggang_Mountains" title="Jinggang Mountains">Jinggang Mountains</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jiangxi" title="Jiangxi">Jiangxi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p64_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p64-97">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jung Chang and Jon Halliday claim that the uprising was in fact sabotaged by Mao to allow him to prevent a group of KMT soldiers from defecting to any other CCP leader.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChangHalliday_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChangHalliday-99">[98]</a></sup> Chang and Halliday also claim that Mao talked the other leaders (including Russian diplomats at the Soviet consulate in Changsha who, Chang and Halliday claim, had been controlling much of the CCP activity) into striking only at Changsha, then abandoning it. Chang and Halliday report a view sent to Moscow by the secretary of the Soviet Consulate in Changsha that the retreat was "the most despicable treachery and cowardice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChangHalliday_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-ChangHalliday-99">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Base_in_Jinggangshan:_1927.E2.80.931928"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Base_in_Jinggangshan:_1927–1928">Base in Jinggangshan: 1927–1928</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao1927.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="594" data-file-width="432" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Mao1927.jpg/170px-Mao1927.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Mao1927.jpg/255px-Mao1927.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Mao1927.jpg/340px-Mao1927.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao1927.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mao in 1927</div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1062260506">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25em; ; background-color: #ACE1AF;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p><span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">革命不是請客吃飯，不是做文章，不是繪畫繡花，不能那樣雅緻，那樣從容不迫，文質彬彬，那樣溫良恭讓。革命是暴動，是一個階級推翻一個階級的暴烈的行動。</span></span><br/><br/>Revolution is not a dinner party, nor an essay, nor a painting, nor a piece of embroidery; it cannot be so refined, so leisurely and gentle, so temperate, kind, courteous, restrained and magnanimous. A revolution is an insurrection, an act of violence by which one class overthrows another.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Mao, February 1927<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>The CCP Central Committee, hiding in Shanghai, expelled Mao from their ranks and from the Hunan Provincial Committee, as punishment for his "military opportunism", for his focus on rural activity, and for being too lenient with "bad gentry". The more orthodox Communists especially regarded the peasants as backward and ridiculed Mao's idea of mobilizing them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mair_2013_p211_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mair_2013_p211-69">[68]</a></sup> They nevertheless adopted three policies he had long championed: the immediate formation of <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_council" title="Workers' council">Workers' councils</a>, the confiscation of all land without exemption, and the rejection of the KMT. Mao's response was to ignore them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> He established a base in <a href="/wiki/Jinggangshan_City" title="Jinggangshan City">Jinggangshan City</a>, an area of the Jinggang Mountains, where he united five villages as a self-governing state, and supported the confiscation of land from rich landlords, who were "re-educated" and sometimes executed. He ensured that no massacres took place in the region, and pursued a more lenient approach than that advocated by the Central Committee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> He proclaimed that "Even the lame, the deaf and the blind could all come in useful for the revolutionary struggle", he boosted the army's numbers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p69_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p69-103">[102]</a></sup> incorporating two groups of bandits into his army, building a force of around 1,800 troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> He laid down rules for his soldiers: prompt obedience to orders, all confiscations were to be turned over to the government, and nothing was to be confiscated from poorer peasants. In doing so, he moulded his men into a disciplined, efficient fighting force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p69_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p69-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1062260506" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:25em; ; background-color: #ACE1AF;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<div class="poem">
<p><span title="Chinese-language text"><span lang="zh">敵進我退，<br/>
敵駐我騷，<br/>
敵疲我打，<br/>
敵退我追。</span></span><br/>
<br/>
When the enemy advances, we retreat.<br/>
When the enemy rests, we harass him.<br/>
When the enemy avoids a battle, we attack.<br/>
When the enemy retreats, we advance.
</p>
</div>
</blockquote>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Mao's advice in combating the Kuomintang, 1928<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p70_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p70-105">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="435" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg/220px-Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg/330px-Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bare_foot_revolutionary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chinese Communist revolutionaries in the 1920s</div></div></div>
<p>In spring 1928, the Central Committee ordered Mao's troops to southern Hunan, hoping to spark peasant uprisings. Mao was skeptical, but complied. They reached Hunan, where they were attacked by the KMT and fled after heavy losses. Meanwhile, KMT troops had invaded Jinggangshan, leaving them without a base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> Wandering the countryside, Mao's forces came across a CCP regiment led by General <a href="/wiki/Zhu_De" title="Zhu De">Zhu De</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lin_Biao" title="Lin Biao">Lin Biao</a>; they united, and attempted to retake Jinggangshan. They were initially successful, but the KMT counter-attacked, and pushed the CCP back; over the next few weeks, they fought an entrenched guerrilla war in the mountains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p70_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p70-105">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> The Central Committee again ordered Mao to march to south Hunan, but he refused, and remained at his base. Contrastingly, Zhu complied, and led his armies away. Mao's troops fended the KMT off for 25 days while he left the camp at night to find reinforcements. He reunited with the decimated Zhu's army, and together they returned to Jinggangshan and retook the base. There they were joined by a defecting KMT regiment and <a href="/wiki/Peng_Dehuai" title="Peng Dehuai">Peng Dehuai</a>'s Fifth Red Army. In the mountainous area they were unable to grow enough crops to feed everyone, leading to food shortages throughout the winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_50_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_50-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1928, Mao met and married <a href="/wiki/He_Zizhen" title="He Zizhen">He Zizhen</a>, an 18-year-old revolutionary who would bear him six children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Jiangxi_Soviet_Republic_of_China:_1929.E2.80.931934"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jiangxi_Soviet_Republic_of_China:_1929–1934">Jiangxi Soviet Republic of China: 1929–1934</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao_Zedong_in_Yan%27an.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="382" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mao_Zedong_in_Yan%27an.jpg/220px-Mao_Zedong_in_Yan%27an.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Mao_Zedong_in_Yan%27an.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao_Zedong_in_Yan%27an.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mao in <a href="/wiki/Yan%27an" title="Yan'an">Yan'an</a></div></div></div>
<p>In January 1929, Mao and Zhu evacuated the base with 2,000 men and a further 800 provided by Peng, and took their armies south, to the area around <a href="/wiki/Tonggu_County" title="Tonggu County">Tonggu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xinfeng_County,_Jiangxi" title="Xinfeng County, Jiangxi">Xinfeng</a> in Jiangxi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> The evacuation led to a drop in morale, and many troops became disobedient and began thieving; this worried <a href="/wiki/Li_Lisan" title="Li Lisan">Li Lisan</a> and the Central Committee, who saw Mao's army as <i><a href="/wiki/Lumpenproletariat" title="Lumpenproletariat">lumpenproletariat</a></i>, that were unable to share in proletariat <a href="/wiki/Class_consciousness" title="Class consciousness">class consciousness</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p72_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p72-115">[114]</a></sup> In keeping with orthodox Marxist thought, Li believed that only the urban proletariat could lead a successful revolution, and saw little need for Mao's peasant guerrillas; he ordered Mao to disband his army into units to be sent out to spread the revolutionary message. Mao replied that while he concurred with Li's theoretical position, he would not disband his army nor abandon his base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p72_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p72-115">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Both Li and Mao saw the Chinese revolution as the key to <a href="/wiki/World_revolution" title="World revolution">world revolution</a>, believing that a CCP victory would spark the overthrow of global imperialism and capitalism. In this, they disagreed with the official line of the Soviet government and Comintern. Officials in Moscow desired greater control over the CCP and removed Li from power by calling him to Russia for an inquest into his errors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p75_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p75-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_51_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_51-119">[118]</a></sup> They replaced him with Soviet-educated Chinese Communists, known as the "<a href="/wiki/28_Bolsheviks" title="28 Bolsheviks">28 Bolsheviks</a>", two of whom, <a href="/wiki/Bo_Gu" title="Bo Gu">Bo Gu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Wentian" title="Zhang Wentian">Zhang Wentian</a>, took control of the Central Committee. Mao disagreed with the new leadership, believing they grasped little of the Chinese situation, and he soon emerged as their key rival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p75_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p75-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="242" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg/220px-1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg/330px-1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg/440px-1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1931_military_parade_of_formation_of_Chinese_Soviet_Republic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Military parade on the occasion of the founding of a Chinese Soviet Republic in 1931</div></div></div>
<p>In February 1930, Mao created the Southwest Jiangxi Provincial Soviet Government in the region under his control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> In November, he suffered emotional trauma after his second wife Yang Kaihui and sister were captured and beheaded by KMT general He Jian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Feigon_2002_50_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Feigon_2002_50-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p75_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p75-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schram1966_p153_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schram1966_p153-122">[121]</a></sup> Facing internal problems, members of the Jiangxi Soviet accused him of being too moderate, and hence anti-revolutionary. In December, they tried to overthrow Mao, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Futian_incident" title="Futian incident">Futian incident</a>, during which Mao's loyalists tortured many and executed between 2000 and 3000 dissenters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p76_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p76-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> The CCP Central Committee moved to Jiangxi which it saw as a secure area. In November, it proclaimed Jiangxi to be the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Republic_of_China" title="Soviet Republic of China">Soviet Republic of China</a>, an independent Communist-governed state. Although he was proclaimed Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars, Mao's power was diminished, as his control of the Red Army was allocated to <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">Zhou Enlai</a>. Meanwhile, Mao recovered from <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p77_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p77-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The KMT armies adopted a policy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encirclement_Campaigns" title="Encirclement Campaigns">encirclement and annihilation</a> of the Red armies. Outnumbered, Mao responded with guerrilla tactics influenced by the works of ancient military strategists like <a href="/wiki/Sun_Tzu" title="Sun Tzu">Sun Tzu</a>, but Zhou and the new leadership followed a policy of open confrontation and conventional warfare. In doing so, the Red Army successfully defeated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Encirclement_Campaign_against_Jiangxi_Soviet" title="First Encirclement Campaign against Jiangxi Soviet">the first</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Encirclement_Campaign_against_Jiangxi_Soviet" title="Second Encirclement Campaign against Jiangxi Soviet">second encirclements</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p78_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p78-129">[128]</a></sup> Angered at his armies' failure, Chiang Kai-shek personally arrived to lead the operation. He too faced setbacks and retreated to deal with the <a href="/wiki/Mukden_Incident" title="Mukden Incident">further Japanese incursions into China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p77_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p77-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> As a result of the KMT's change of focus to the defence of China against Japanese expansionism, the Red Army was able to expand its area of control, eventually encompassing a population of 3 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carter1976_p78_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carter1976_p78-129">[128]</a></sup> Mao proceeded with his land reform program. In November 1931 he announced the start of a "land verification project" which was expanded in June 1933.
